<p>The <b>University of Florida</b> (commonly referred to as <b>Florida</b> or <b>UF</b>) is an American <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Land-grant_university" title="Land-grant university">land-grant</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_grant_colleges" title="Sea grant colleges">sea-grant</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_grant_colleges" title="Space grant colleges">space-grant</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university">research university</a> on a 2,000-acre (8.1 km<sup>2</sup>) campus in <a href="/wiki/Gainesville,_Florida" title="Gainesville, Florida">Gainesville, Florida</a>. It is a senior member of the <a href="/wiki/State_University_System_of_Florida" title="State University System of Florida">State University System of Florida</a> and traces its origins to 1853,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[7]</a></sup> and has operated continuously on its Gainesville campus since September 1906.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The University of Florida is one of sixty-two elected member institutions of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> (AAU), the association of preeminent North American research universities, and the only AAU member university in Florida.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[9]</a></sup> The University is classified as a <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Classification_of_Institutions_of_Higher_Education" title="Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education">Research University with Very High Research</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Foundation_for_the_Advancement_of_Teaching" title="Carnegie Foundation for the Advancement of Teaching">Carnegie Foundation for the Advancement of Teaching</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[10]</a></sup> After the Florida state legislature's creation of performance standards in 2013, the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Board_of_Governors" title="Florida Board of Governors">Florida Board of Governors</a> designated the University of Florida as one of the two "preeminent universities" among the twelve universities of the State University System of Florida.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup> For 2018, <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> ranked Florida as the ninth (tied) best public university in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-colleges.usnews.rankingsandreviews.com_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-colleges.usnews.rankingsandreviews.com-15">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>The university is accredited by the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Association_of_Colleges_and_Schools" title="Southern Association of Colleges and Schools">Southern Association of Colleges and Schools</a> (SACS). It is the third largest Florida university by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_largest_United_States_university_campuses_by_enrollment" title="List of largest United States university campuses by enrollment">student population</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sun_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-sun-16">[14]</a></sup> and is the eighth largest single-campus university in the United States with 49,913 students enrolled for the fall 2012 semester.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oipr-enrollment_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-oipr-enrollment-17">[15]</a></sup> The University of Florida is home to sixteen academic colleges and more than 150 research centers and institutes. It offers multiple graduate professional programs—including <a href="/wiki/Business_administration" title="Business administration">business administration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Law" title="Law">law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dentistry" title="Dentistry">dentistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Veterinary_medicine" title="Veterinary medicine">veterinary medicine</a>—on one contiguous campus, and administers 123 <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master's degree">master's degree</a> programs and seventy-six <a href="/wiki/Doctorate" title="Doctorate">doctoral degree</a> programs in eighty-seven schools and departments.</p>
<p>The University of Florida's intercollegiate sports teams, commonly known by their "<a href="/wiki/Florida_Gators" title="Florida Gators">Florida Gators</a>" nickname, compete in <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a> (NCAA) <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">Division I</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference" title="Southeastern Conference">Southeastern Conference</a> (SEC). In their 108-year history, the university's varsity sports teams have won thirty-nine national team championships, thirty-four of which are NCAA titles, and Gator athletes have won 275 individual national championships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_University_of_Florida" title="History of the University of Florida">History of the University of Florida</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dsg_UF_Century_Tower_20050507.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="854" data-file-width="536" height="319" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Dsg_UF_Century_Tower_20050507.jpg/200px-Dsg_UF_Century_Tower_20050507.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Dsg_UF_Century_Tower_20050507.jpg/300px-Dsg_UF_Century_Tower_20050507.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Dsg_UF_Century_Tower_20050507.jpg/400px-Dsg_UF_Century_Tower_20050507.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dsg_UF_Century_Tower_20050507.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Century_Tower_(University_of_Florida)" title="Century Tower (University of Florida)">Century Tower</a>, begun in 1953, to commemorate the 100th anniversary of the founding of university and as a tribute to the alumni who perished in both <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The University of Florida traces its origins to 1853, when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Florida_Seminary" title="East Florida Seminary">East Florida Seminary</a>, the oldest of the University of Florida's four predecessor institutions, was founded in <a href="/wiki/Ocala,_Florida" title="Ocala, Florida">Ocala, Florida</a>.</p>
<p>On January 6, 1853, Governor <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Brown_(Florida_politician)" title="Thomas Brown (Florida politician)">Thomas Brown</a> signed a bill that provided public support for higher education in Florida.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[17]</a></sup> Gilbert Kingsbury was the first person to take advantage of the legislation, and established the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_University_of_Florida" title="History of the University of Florida">East Florida Seminary</a>, which operated until the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">Civil War</a> in 1861. The East Florida Seminary was Florida's first state-supported institution of higher learning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>James Henry Roper, an educator from <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Florida_Senate" title="Florida Senate">state senator</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alachua_County" title="Alachua County">Alachua County</a>, had opened a school in Gainesville, the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_University_of_Florida" title="History of the University of Florida">Gainesville Academy</a>, in 1858. In 1866,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[19]</a></sup> Roper offered his land and school to the State of Florida in exchange for the East Florida Seminary's relocation to Gainesville.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>The second major precursor to the University of Florida was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Florida_Agricultural_College" title="Florida Agricultural College">Florida Agricultural College</a>, established at <a href="/wiki/Lake_City,_Florida" title="Lake City, Florida">Lake City</a> by Jordan Probst in 1884. Florida Agricultural College became the state's first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Land-grant_college" title="Land-grant college">land-grant college</a> under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morrill_Act" title="Morrill Act">Morrill Act</a>. In 1903, the Florida Legislature, desiring to expand the school's outlook and curriculum beyond its agricultural and engineering origins, changed the name of Florida Agricultural College to the "University of Florida," a name the school would hold for only two years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id='"University_of_the_State_of_Florida"'></span><span class="mw-headline" id=".22University_of_the_State_of_Florida.22">"University of the State of Florida"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title='Edit section: "University of the State of Florida"'>edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1905, the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Legislature" title="Florida Legislature">Florida Legislature</a> passed the <a href="/wiki/Henry_Holland_Buckman" title="Henry Holland Buckman">Buckman Act</a>, which consolidated the state's publicly supported higher education institutions. The member of the legislature who wrote the act, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Holland_Buckman" title="Henry Holland Buckman">Henry Holland Buckman</a>, later became the namesake of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buckman_Hall" title="Buckman Hall">Buckman Hall</a>, one of the university's oldest buildings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[22]</a></sup> The Buckman Act organized the <a href="/wiki/State_University_System_of_Florida" title="State University System of Florida">State University System of Florida</a> and created the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Board_of_Control" title="Florida Board of Control">Florida Board of Control</a> to govern the system. The act abolished the six pre-existing state-supported institutions of higher education, and consolidated the assets and academic programs of four of them to form the new "<a href="/wiki/History_of_the_University_of_Florida" title="History of the University of Florida">University of the State of Florida</a>." The four predecessor institutions consolidated to form the new university included the <b>University of Florida at Lake City</b> (formerly Florida Agricultural College) in <a href="/wiki/Lake_City,_Florida" title="Lake City, Florida">Lake City</a>, the <b>East Florida Seminary</b> in Gainesville, the <b>St. Petersburg Normal and Industrial School</b> in <a href="/wiki/St._Petersburg,_Florida" title="St. Petersburg, Florida">St. Petersburg</a>, and the <b>South Florida Military College</b> in <a href="/wiki/Bartow,_Florida" title="Bartow, Florida">Bartow</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Buckman Act also consolidated the colleges and schools into three institutions segregated by race and gender—the University of the State of Florida for white men, the <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_University" title="Florida State University">Florida Female College</a> for white women, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Florida_A%26M" title="Florida A&amp;M">State Normal School for Colored Students</a> for African-American men and women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-State_Library_and_Archives_of_Florida_-_The_Florida_Memory_Project_Timeline_.28see_1905.29_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-State_Library_and_Archives_of_Florida_-_The_Florida_Memory_Project_Timeline_.28see_1905.29-26">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>The City of Gainesville, led by its Mayor <a href="/wiki/William_Reuben_Thomas" title="William Reuben Thomas">William Reuben Thomas</a>, campaigned to be home to the new university.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup> On July 6, 1905, the Board of Control selected <a href="/wiki/Gainesville,_Florida" title="Gainesville, Florida">Gainesville</a> for the new university campus. <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Sledd" title="Andrew Sledd">Andrew Sledd</a>, president of the pre-existing <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_University_of_Florida" title="History of the University of Florida">University of Florida at Lake City</a>, was selected to be the first president of the new University of the State of Florida. The 1905-1906 academic year was a year of transition; the new University of the State of Florida was legally created, but operated on the campus of the old University of Florida in Lake City until the first buildings on the new campus in Gainesville were complete. Architect William A. Edwards designed the first official campus buildings in the <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">Collegiate Gothic</a> style. Classes began on the new Gainesville campus on September 26, 1906, with 102 students enrolled.</p>
<p>In 1909, the school's name was simplified from the "University of the State of Florida" to the "University of Florida."</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Alligator" title="Alligator">alligator</a> was incidentally chosen as the school mascot in 1911, after a local vendor ordered and sold school pennants imprinted with an alligator emblem. The school colors, orange and blue, are a reference to the region's heritage and an homage to the Scottish and Ulster-Scots Presbyterian heritage of the original founders of Gainesville and Alachua County, most of whom were settlers from North Carolina whose ancestors were primarily Presbyterians of Scottish descent who had come to America from <a href="/wiki/County_Down" title="County Down">County Down</a> and <a href="/wiki/County_Antrim" title="County Antrim">County Antrim</a> in what has since become <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, while some had come directly from the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Lowlands" title="Scottish Lowlands">Scottish Lowlands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MurphreeStatue.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="500" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/MurphreeStatue.jpg/220px-MurphreeStatue.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/MurphreeStatue.jpg/330px-MurphreeStatue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/MurphreeStatue.jpg/440px-MurphreeStatue.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MurphreeStatue.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Statue of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albert_Murphree" title="Albert Murphree">Albert Murphree</a>, the second president of the university.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="College_reorganization">College reorganization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: College reorganization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1909, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albert_Murphree" title="Albert Murphree">Albert Murphree</a> was appointed the university's second president, and organized several of the colleges of the university, increased enrollment from under 200 to over 2,000, and he was instrumental in the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Blue_Key" title="Florida Blue Key">Florida Blue Key</a> leadership society. Murphree is the only University of Florida president honored with a statue on the campus.</p>
<p>In 1924, the Florida Legislature mandated women of a "mature age" (at least twenty-one years old) who had completed sixty semester hours from a "reputable educational institution" would be allowed to enroll during regular semesters at the University of Florida in programs that were unavailable at Florida State College for Women. Before this, only the summer semester was coeducational, to accommodate women teachers who wanted to further their education during the summer break.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lassie_Goodbread-Black" title="Lassie Goodbread-Black">Lassie Goodbread-Black</a> from Lake City became the first woman to enroll at the University of Florida, in the College of Agriculture in 1925.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/John_J._Tigert" title="John J. Tigert">John J. Tigert</a> became the third university president in 1928. Disgusted by the under-the-table payments being made by universities to athletes, Tigert established the grant-in-aid <a href="/wiki/Athletic_scholarship" title="Athletic scholarship">athletic scholarship</a> program in the early 1930s, which was the genesis of the modern athletic scholarship plan used by the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post_World_War_II">Post World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Post World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Beginning in 1946, there was dramatically increased interest among male applicants who wanted to attend the University of Florida, mostly returning <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> veterans who could attend college under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GI_Bill_of_Rights" title="GI Bill of Rights">GI Bill of Rights</a> (Servicemen's Readjustment Act). Unable to immediately accommodate this increased demand, the Florida Board of Control opened the <b>Tallahassee Branch of the University of Florida</b> on the campus of Florida State College for Women in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tallahassee" title="Tallahassee">Tallahassee</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup> By the end of the 1946–47 school year, 954 men were enrolled at the Tallahassee Branch. The following semester, the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Legislature" title="Florida Legislature">Florida Legislature</a> returned the Florida State College for Women to coeducational status and renamed it <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_University" title="Florida State University">Florida State University</a>. These events also opened up all of the colleges that comprise the University of Florida to female students. African-American students were allowed to enroll starting in 1958.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/UF_Health_Shands_Hospital" title="UF Health Shands Hospital">Shands Hospital</a> opened in 1958 along with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_College_of_Medicine" title="University of Florida College of Medicine">University of Florida College of Medicine</a> to join the established <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_College_of_Pharmacy" title="University of Florida College of Pharmacy">College of Pharmacy</a>. Rapid campus expansion began in the 1950s and continues today.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>The University of Florida is one of two Florida public universities, along with <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_University" title="Florida State University">Florida State University</a>, to be designated as a "preeminent university" by Florida senate bill 1076, enacted by the Florida legislature and signed into law by the governor in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup> As a result, the preeminent universities receive additional funding intended to improve the academics and national reputation of higher education within the state of Florida.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_and_international_prominence">National and international prominence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: National and international prominence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Historic_Layout_University_of_Florida.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1350" data-file-width="2033" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Historic_Layout_University_of_Florida.jpg/220px-Historic_Layout_University_of_Florida.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Historic_Layout_University_of_Florida.jpg/330px-Historic_Layout_University_of_Florida.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Historic_Layout_University_of_Florida.jpg/440px-Historic_Layout_University_of_Florida.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Historic_Layout_University_of_Florida.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The University of Florida campus in 1916, looking southwest.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1985, the University of Florida was invited to join the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> (AAU), an organization of sixty-two academically prominent public and private research universities in the United States and Canada. Florida is one of the seventeen public, land-grant universities that belong to the AAU. In 2009, President <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Machen" title="Bernie Machen">Bernie Machen</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_Board_of_Trustees" title="University of Florida Board of Trustees">University of Florida Board of Trustees</a> announced a major policy transition for the university. The Board of Trustees supported the reduction in the number of undergraduates and the shift of financial and other academic resources to graduate education and research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup> In 2017 the University of Florida became the first university in the state of Florida to crack the top ten best public universities according to U.S. News.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[39]</a></sup> As of 2016 the University of Florida generated $791.3 Million in Research Expenditures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ufl.edu_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-ufl.edu-42">[40]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2016, the University of Florida had 35,043 undergraduate students, and 52,286 students in total. The ratio of women to men is 55:45, and 32 percent are graduate and professional students. Professional degree programs include architecture, dentistry, law, medicine, pharmacy and veterinary medicine. Minority populations constitute about 36 percent of the student body, with 6.5 percent African-Americans, 21.0 percent Hispanics, 0.5 percent Native American, and 7.9 percent Asian-Americans or Pacific Islanders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2016, the total number of International students attending the university was 5,169.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>The University of Florida is ranked second overall in the United States for the number of bachelor's degrees awarded to African-Americans, and third overall for Hispanics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup> The university ranks fifth overall in the number of doctoral degrees awarded to African-Americans, and second overall for Hispanics, and third overall in number of professional degrees awarded to African-Americans, and second overall for Hispanics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup> The university offers multiple graduate programs—-including engineering, business, law and medicine—-on one contiguous campus, and coordinates 123 master's degree programs and 76 doctoral degree programs in 87 schools and departments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup></p>

<p>In its 2018 edition, <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> (USN&amp;WR) ranked the University of Florida as tied for the 9th-best public university in the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-colleges.usnews.rankingsandreviews.com_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-colleges.usnews.rankingsandreviews.com-15">[13]</a></sup> and tied for 42nd overall among all national universities, public and private.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USNWR_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-USNWR-63">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many of the University of Florida's graduate schools have received top-50 rankings from <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i> with the school of education 30th, Florida's Hough school of business tied for 37th nationally, Florida's medical school (research) 43rd (tie), the engineering school 43rd (tie), the Levin college of law 47th (tie), and the nursing school 48th (tie) in the 2016 rankings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USNWR_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-USNWR-63">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Florida's graduate programs ranked for 2016 by <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i> in the nation's top 50 were audiology 7th, analytical chemistry 8th, occupational therapy 10th, criminology 12th, physical therapy 12th, pharmacy 9th, veterinary medicine 14th, speech-language pathology 15th, physician assistant 27th, healthcare management 29th, public health 30th, statistics 30th, chemistry 35th, physics 36th, clinical psychology 37th, psychology 40th, history 46th, computer science 48th, economics 48th, and political science 50th.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USNWR_63-2"><a href="#cite_note-USNWR-63">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i> ranked the engineering school 38th nationally,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup> with its programs in biological engineering ranked 3rd,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> materials engineering 11th,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> industrial engineering 13th,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> aerospace engineering 26th,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup> chemical engineering 28th,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> environmental engineering 30th,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup> computer engineering 31st,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup> civil engineering 32nd,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup> electrical engineering 34th,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup> mechanical engineering 44th.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 2015 <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></i> list assessed the University of Florida as 90th among world universities and 45th in the United States in 2016, based on overall research output and faculty awards. In 2016, <i><a href="/wiki/Washington_Monthly" title="Washington Monthly">Washington Monthly</a></i> ranked the University of Florida 18th among national universities, with criteria based on research, community service, and social mobility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup> The lowest national ranking received by the university from a major publication comes from Forbes which ranked the university 78th in the nation in August 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup> This ranking focuses mainly on net positive financial impact, in contrast to other rankings, and generally ranks liberal arts colleges above most research universities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, Florida Governor Rick Scott publicly announced his support for the University of Florida to ascend into the top ten among public universities, as measured by <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup> He called for additional funding to decrease the student-faculty ratio at the university.</p>
<p>Florida was ranked 14th in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Princeton_Review" title="The Princeton Review">The Princeton Review</a>'</i>s 2015 list of top party schools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup> It also was named the number one vegan-friendly school for 2014, according to a survey conducted by <a href="/wiki/People_for_the_Ethical_Treatment_of_Animals" title="People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals">PETA</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>On Forbes’ 2016 list of Best Value Public Colleges, UF was ranked second. It was also ranked third on Forbes’ Overall Best Value Colleges Nationwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_academic_divisions">Colleges and academic divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Colleges and academic divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The University of Florida is divided into 16 colleges and more than 150 research, service and education centers, bureaus and institutes, offering more than 100 undergraduate majors and 200 graduate degrees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup></p>

<p>For the class of 2021, there were over 34,000 applicants and 13,214 were accepted for summer and fall. The average GPA for the admitted students was a 4.4, the average SAT was a 1349 out of 1600, and the average ACT was a 30 out of 36.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ending_early_decision">Ending early decision</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Ending early decision">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2007, the University of Florida joined the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Virginia" title="University of Virginia">University of Virginia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill" title="University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill">University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton University</a> when they announced they were discontinuing their <a href="/wiki/Early_decision" title="Early decision">early decision</a> admissions to foster economic diversity in their student bodies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup> These universities assert early decision admissions forces students to accept an offer of admission before evaluating the <a href="/wiki/Student_financial_aid_(United_States)" title="Student financial aid (United States)">financial aid</a> offers from multiple universities. The university's single application deadline is November 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Honors_program">Honors program</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Honors program">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UF_NewHume.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="11869" height="54" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/UF_NewHume.jpg/250px-UF_NewHume.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/UF_NewHume.jpg/375px-UF_NewHume.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/UF_NewHume.jpg/500px-UF_NewHume.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UF_NewHume.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Honors Residential College at <a href="/wiki/Hume_Hall" title="Hume Hall">Hume Hall</a> provides residential and classroom facilities for students in the Honors Program.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The University of Florida has an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honors_course" title="Honors course">honors program</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Honors_Program_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Honors_Program-89">[87]</a></sup> After gaining acceptance to the university, students must apply separately to the Honors Program and demonstrate significant academic achievement to be accepted. There are over 100 courses offered exclusively to students in this program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup> In 2011, more than 1900 students applied for 700 available seats. The Honors Program also offers housing for freshman in the <a href="/wiki/Hume_Hall" title="Hume Hall">Honors Residential College at Hume Hall</a>. The program also offers special <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scholarships" title="Scholarships">scholarships</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internships" title="Internships">internships</a>, research, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Study_abroad" title="Study abroad">study abroad</a> opportunities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Scholarships">Scholarships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Scholarships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Lombardi Scholars Program, created in 2002 and named in honor of the university's ninth president <a href="/wiki/John_V._Lombardi" title="John V. Lombardi">John V. Lombardi</a>, is a merit scholarship for Florida students. The scholarship offers $2,700 a semester for eight to ten semesters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>The J. Wayne Reitz Scholars Program, created in 1997 and named in honor of the university's fifth president <a href="/wiki/J._Wayne_Reitz" title="J. Wayne Reitz">J. Wayne Reitz</a>, is a leadership and merit-based scholarship for Florida students. Its yearly $2,500 stipend may be renewed for up to three years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Machen Florida Opportunity Scholars Program was created in 2005. This is a full grant and scholarship financial aid package designed to help new, low-income UF students that are the first to attend college in their families. Every year, 300 scholarships are awarded to incoming freshmen with an average family income of $18,408.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UF_RinkerHall.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/UF_RinkerHall.jpg/220px-UF_RinkerHall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/UF_RinkerHall.jpg/330px-UF_RinkerHall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/UF_RinkerHall.jpg/440px-UF_RinkerHall.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UF_RinkerHall.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Opened in 2003, <a href="/wiki/Rinker_School_of_Building_Construction" title="Rinker School of Building Construction">Rinker Hall</a> was the first building on campus to receive <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">LEED</a> recognition. Since opening, other new and renovated buildings on campus have also received certification.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2005, the University of Florida became a <a href="/wiki/National_Audubon_Society" title="National Audubon Society">Certified Audubon Cooperative Sanctuary</a> for environmental and wildlife management, resource conservation, environmental education, waste management, and outreach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>Through long-term environmental initiatives, the University of Florida created an Office of Sustainability in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aashe.org_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-aashe.org-99">[97]</a></sup> Their mission is to improve environmental sustainability in many areas on campus. They have stated their goals are to produce zero waste by 2015 and to achieve Carbon Neutrality by 2025.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aashe.org_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-aashe.org-99">[97]</a></sup> Recently the university appointed a new sustainability director. Florida received a "B+" grade on the 2009 College Sustainability Report Card for its environmental and sustainability initiatives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2009_College_Sustainability_Report_Card_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-2009_College_Sustainability_Report_Card-100">[98]</a></sup> In 2009, "B+" was the second highest grade awarded by the Sustainable Endowments Institute.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Satellite_facilities">Satellite facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Satellite facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The university maintains a number of facilities apart from its main campus. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J._Hillis_Miller_Health_Science_Center" title="J. Hillis Miller Health Science Center">J. Hillis Miller Health Science Center</a> also has a teaching hospital located at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UF_Health_at_Jacksonville" title="UF Health at Jacksonville">UF Health at Jacksonville</a>, which serves as the <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Jacksonville, Florida">Jacksonville</a> campus for the University's <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_College_of_Medicine-Jacksonville" title="University of Florida College of Medicine-Jacksonville">College of Medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_College_of_Nursing" title="University of Florida College of Nursing">College of Nursing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_College_of_Pharmacy" title="University of Florida College of Pharmacy">College of Pharmacy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jaxshands_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-jaxshands-101">[99]</a></sup> A number of residencies are also offered at this facility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jaxshands_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-jaxshands-101">[99]</a></sup> The University's College of Pharmacy also maintains campuses in <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">Orlando</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Jacksonville, Florida">Jacksonville</a>, and <a href="/wiki/St._Petersburg,_Florida" title="St. Petersburg, Florida">St. Petersburg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[100]</a></sup> The College of Dentistry maintains clinics in <a href="/wiki/Hialeah,_Florida" title="Hialeah, Florida">Hialeah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naples,_Florida" title="Naples, Florida">Naples</a>, and <a href="/wiki/St._Petersburg,_Florida" title="St. Petersburg, Florida">St. Petersburg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>The university's <a href="/wiki/Warrington_College_of_Business" title="Warrington College of Business">Warrington College of Business</a> established programs in <a href="/wiki/South_Florida" title="South Florida">South Florida</a> in 2004, and recently built a 6,100-square-foot (570 m<sup>2</sup>) facility in <a href="/wiki/Sunrise,_Florida" title="Sunrise, Florida">Sunrise, Florida</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Food_and_Agricultural_Sciences" title="Institute of Food and Agricultural Sciences">Institute of Food and Agricultural Sciences</a> has <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cooperative_extension_service" title="Cooperative extension service">extensions</a> in each of the 67 counties in Florida, and 13 research and education centers with a total of 19 locations throughout the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[103]</a></sup> In 2005, the university established the Beijing Center for International Studies in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> that offers research facilities, offices, and degree opportunities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sid_Martin_Biotechnology_Incubator" title="Sid Martin Biotechnology Incubator">Sid Martin Biotechnology Incubator</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UF_Cancer_Genetics_Complex.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/UF_Cancer_Genetics_Complex.JPG/220px-UF_Cancer_Genetics_Complex.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/UF_Cancer_Genetics_Complex.JPG/330px-UF_Cancer_Genetics_Complex.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/UF_Cancer_Genetics_Complex.JPG/440px-UF_Cancer_Genetics_Complex.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UF_Cancer_Genetics_Complex.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_Cancer_and_Genetics_Research_Complex" title="University of Florida Cancer and Genetics Research Complex">University of Florida Cancer and Genetics Research Complex</a> is one of several research facilities at the university</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The University of Florida is one of the nation's largest research universities. According to a 2011 study by the university's <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Food_and_Agricultural_Sciences" title="Institute of Food and Agricultural Sciences">Institute of Food and Agricultural Sciences</a>, the university contributed $8.76 billion to Florida's economy and was responsible for over 100,000 jobs in the 2009–10 fiscal year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[105]</a></sup> The Milken Institute named Florida one of the top-five U.S. institutions in the transfer of <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a> research to the marketplace (2006).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup> Some 50 biotechnology companies have resulted from faculty research programs. Florida consistently ranks among the top 10 universities in licensing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MediaGuide_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-MediaGuide-109">[107]</a></sup> Royalty and licensing income includes the glaucoma drug <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trusopt" title="Trusopt">Trusopt</a>, the sports drink <a href="/wiki/Gatorade" title="Gatorade">Gatorade</a>, and the Sentricon <a href="/wiki/Termite" title="Termite">termite</a> elimination system. The Institute of Food and Agricultural Sciences is ranked No. 1 by the NSF in Research and Development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup> Florida ranked seventh among all private and public universities for the total number of patents awarded for 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MediaGuide_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-MediaGuide-109">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>The University of Florida was awarded $791 million in research expenditures in sponsored research in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup> Research includes diverse areas such as health-care and citrus production (the world's largest citrus research center). In 2002, Florida began leading six other universities under a $15 million <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> grant to work on space-related research during a five-year period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[110]</a></sup> The university's partnership with Spain helped to create the <a href="/wiki/Gran_Telescopio_Canarias" title="Gran Telescopio Canarias">world's largest single-aperture optical telescope</a> in the Canary Islands (the cost was $93 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MediaGuide_109-2"><a href="#cite_note-MediaGuide-109">[107]</a></sup> Plans are also under way for the University of Florida to construct a 50,000-square-foot (4,600 m<sup>2</sup>) research facility in collaboration with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burnham_Institute_for_Medical_Research" title="Burnham Institute for Medical Research">Burnham Institute for Medical Research</a> that will be in the center of <a href="/wiki/University_of_Central_Florida" title="University of Central Florida">University of Central Florida</a>'s Health Sciences Campus in <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">Orlando, Florida</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup> Research will include diabetes, aging, genetics and cancer.</p>
<p>The University of Florida has made great strides in the space sciences over the last decade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Press_-_Caltech_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Press_-_Caltech-114">[112]</a></sup> The Astronomy Department's focus on the development of image-detection devices has led to increases in funding, telescope time, and significant scholarly achievements. Faculty members in organic chemistry have made notable discoveries in astrobiology, while faculty members in physics have participated actively in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laser_Interferometer_Gravitational-Wave_Observatory" title="Laser Interferometer Gravitational-Wave Observatory">Laser Interferometer Gravitational-Wave Observatory</a> project, the largest and most ambitious project ever funded by the NSF.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Press_-_Caltech_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-Press_-_Caltech-114">[112]</a></sup> Through the Department of Mechanical and Aerospace Engineering, the University of Florida is the lead institution on the NASA University Research, Engineering, and Technology Institute (URETI) for Future Space Transport project to develop the next generation space shuttle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition, the university also performs diabetes research in a statewide screening program that has been sponsored by a $10 million grant from the <a href="/wiki/American_Diabetes_Association" title="American Diabetes Association">American Diabetes Association</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup> The University of Florida also houses one of the world's leading lightning research teams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MediaGuide_109-3"><a href="#cite_note-MediaGuide-109">[107]</a></sup> University scientists have started a biofuels pilot plant designed to test ethanol-producing technology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MediaGuide_109-4"><a href="#cite_note-MediaGuide-109">[107]</a></sup> The university is also host to a <a href="/wiki/UF_Training_Reactor" title="UF Training Reactor">nuclear research reactor</a> known for its Neutron Activation Analysis Laboratory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup> In addition, the University of Florida is the first American university to receive a <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> grant to house a <a href="/wiki/Jean_Monnet" title="Jean Monnet">Jean Monnet</a> Centre of Excellence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2012, the University of Florida had more than $750 million in new research facilities recently completed or under construction, including the Nanoscale Research Facility, the Pathogens Research Facility <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[117]</a></sup> and the Biomedical Sciences Building.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[119]</a></sup> Additionally, Innovation Square, a 24/7 live/work/play research environment being developed along Southwest Second Avenue between the University of Florida campus and downtown Gainesville, recently broke ground and plans to open next fall. The university's Office of Technology Licensing will relocate to Innovation Square, joining Florida Innovation Hub, a business "super-incubator designed to promote the development of new high-tech companies based on the university's research programs. Innovation Square will include retail space, restaurants and local businesses, and residential space.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_International_Center_for_Lightning_Research_and_Testing">The International Center for Lightning Research and Testing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: The International Center for Lightning Research and Testing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(November 2015)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Florida has more <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">lightning</a> than any other U.S. state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup> UF sponsors the International Center for Lightning Research and Testing (ICLRT), which occupies over 100 acres (40 ha) at the <a href="/wiki/Camp_Blanding" title="Camp Blanding">Camp Blanding</a> Army National Guard Base.,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup> about 25 miles (45 km) northeast of UF's campus in Gainesville, Florida. One of their primary research tools is lightning initiation from overhead thunderclouds, using the triggered lightning rocket-and-wire technique. Small sounding rockets, connected to long copper wires, are fired into likely lightning storm <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cumulonimbus" title="Cumulonimbus">cumulonimbus</a> clouds. When the rocket—or its wire—is struck by lightning, the passing of the high-voltage lightning strike down the wire vaporizes it as the lightning travels to the ground. Undergraduate and graduate research in UF's Department of Electrical and Computer Engineering's Lightning Research Group is used to increase new fundamental knowledge about lightning-based phenomena.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="UF_Health">UF Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: UF Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>University of Florida Health has two campuses in Gainesville and Jacksonville. It includes two teaching hospitals and two specialty hospitals, as well as the colleges of Dentistry, Medicine, Nursing, Pharmacy, Public Health and Health Professions, and Veterinary Medicine, including a large animal hospital and a small animal hospital. The system also encompasses six UF research institutes: the Clinical and Translational Science Institute, the Evelyn F. and William L. McKnight Brain Institute, the Genetics Institute, the UF Health Cancer Center, the Institute on Aging and the Emerging Pathogens Institute. UF Health is the only academic health center in the United States with six health-related colleges on a single, contiguous campus.</p>
<p>Patient-care services are provided through the private, not-for-profit UF Health Shands family of hospitals and programs. UF Health Shands Hospital in Gainesville includes UF Health Shands Children's Hospital and UF Health Shands Cancer Hospital. The specialty hospitals, UF Health Shands Rehab Hospital and UF Health Shands Psychiatric Hospital, are also in Gainesville. UF Health Jacksonville is the system's northeast Florida center.</p>
<p>UF Health has a network of outpatient rehabilitation centers, UF Health Rehab Centers, and two home-health agencies, UF Health Shands HomeCare; as well as more than 80 UF physician outpatient practices in north central and northeast Florida. UF Health is affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Veterans_Affairs" title="United States Department of Veterans Affairs">Veterans Affairs</a> hospitals in Gainesville and North Florida/South Georgia.</p>
<p>In all, 6,159 students are enrolled in all six of the colleges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> is also part of the Health Science Center and is the most comprehensive program of its kind in the world. The Institute comprises 300 faculty members from 10 colleges, and 51 departments campus-wide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MediaGuide_109-5"><a href="#cite_note-MediaGuide-109">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>The University of Florida is a winner of the <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health" title="National Institutes of Health">National Institutes of Health</a> Clinical and Translational Science Award and member of the NIH national consortium of medical research institutions.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="UF_Health_Jacksonville">UF Health Jacksonville</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: UF Health Jacksonville">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a class="external text" href="http://www.hscj.ufl.edu/" rel="nofollow">UF Health Jacksonville</a> is an academic health center with three UF colleges, Medicine, Nursing and Pharmacy, as well as a network of primary and specialty care centers in northeast Florida and southeast Georgia.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Orlando_Health">Orlando Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Orlando Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2010, <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Health" title="Orlando Health">Orlando Health</a> and UF Health teamed up to form joint clinical programs in the areas of pediatrics, neuroscience, oncology, women's health, transplantation and cardiovascular medicine. The partnership provides undergraduate and graduate medical residency and fellowship training opportunities at Orlando Health, and will allow Orlando Health physicians and patients to be part of clinical trials through UF's clinical research program.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="UF_Health_Cancer_Center_at_Orlando_Health">UF Health Cancer Center at Orlando Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: UF Health Cancer Center at Orlando Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>UF Health Cancer Center at Orlando Health<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup> launched in January 2014. The center focuses on developing safe, individualized molecular-based targeted oncology therapies to improve patient outcomes in Florida. The joint oncology program offers clinical trial collaborations and comprehensive cancer services customized to the patient by combining physicians and the collective strengths of UF Health and Orlando Health.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Participation_in_the_Large_Hadron_Collider">Participation in the Large Hadron Collider</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Participation in the Large Hadron Collider">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A team of UF physicists has a leading role in one of the two major experiments planned for the <a href="/wiki/Large_Hadron_Collider" title="Large Hadron Collider">Large Hadron Collider</a>, a 17-mile (27 km)-long, $5 billion, super-cooled underground tunnel outside Geneva, Switzerland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup> More than 30 university physicists, postdoctoral associates, graduate students and now undergraduates are involved in the collider's <a href="/wiki/Compact_Muon_Solenoid" title="Compact Muon Solenoid">Compact Muon Solenoid</a> (CMS) experiment, one of its two major experiments. About 10 are stationed in Geneva. The group is the largest from any university in the U.S. to participate in the CMS experiment. The UF team designed and oversaw development of a major detector within the CMS. The detector, the Muon system, is intended to capture subatomic particles called muons, which are heavier cousins of electrons. Among other efforts, UF scientists analyzed about 100 of the 400 detector chambers placed within the Muon system to be sure they were functioning properly. Scientists from the University of Florida group played a central role in the discovery of the Higgs particle. The bulk of the UF research was funded by the U.S. Department of Energy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Partnership_with_Zhejiang_University">Partnership with Zhejiang University</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Partnership with Zhejiang University">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In July 2008, the University of Florida teamed up with the <a href="/wiki/Zhejiang_University" title="Zhejiang University">Zhejiang University</a> to research sustainable solutions to the Earth's energy issues. Overall a Joint Research Center of Clean Sustainable Energy among the Florida Institute for Sustainable Energy, at UF, and the State Key Lab of Clean Energy Utilization and the Institute for Thermal Power Engineering, at Zhejiang University will collaborate to work on this pressing issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="SECU:_SEC_Academic_Initiative">SECU: SEC Academic Initiative</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: SECU: SEC Academic Initiative">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The University of Florida is a member of the SEC Academic Consortium. Now renamed the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference#The_formation_of_SECU_and_SEC_academic_network" title="Southeastern Conference">SECU</a>, the initiative was a collaborative endeavor designed to promote research, scholarship and achievement amongst the member universities in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southeastern_conference" title="Southeastern conference">Southeastern conference</a>. Along with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Georgia" title="University of Georgia">University of Georgia</a>, University of Florida, <a href="/wiki/Vanderbilt_University" title="Vanderbilt University">Vanderbilt University</a> and other SEC institutions, SECU formed its mission to bolster collaborative academic endeavors of <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference#Member_universities" title="Southeastern Conference">Southeastern Conference universities</a>. Its goals include highlighting the endeavors and achievements of SEC <a href="/wiki/Faculty_(academic_staff)" title="Faculty (academic staff)">faculty</a>, students and its universities and advancing the academic reputation of SEC universities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, the University of Florida was part in the SEC Symposium in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlanta,_Georgia" title="Atlanta, Georgia">Atlanta, Georgia</a> which was organized and led by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Georgia" title="University of Georgia">University of Georgia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Georgia#UGA_Bioenergy_Systems_Research_Institute" title="University of Georgia">UGA Bioenergy Systems Research Institute</a>. The topic of the Symposium was, the "Impact of the Southeast in the World's Renewable Energy Future."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UFHistoricBuildingSmathersLibraryEastInteriorSpecialCollectionsRoom.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="2400" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/UFHistoricBuildingSmathersLibraryEastInteriorSpecialCollectionsRoom.JPG/220px-UFHistoricBuildingSmathersLibraryEastInteriorSpecialCollectionsRoom.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/UFHistoricBuildingSmathersLibraryEastInteriorSpecialCollectionsRoom.JPG/330px-UFHistoricBuildingSmathersLibraryEastInteriorSpecialCollectionsRoom.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/UFHistoricBuildingSmathersLibraryEastInteriorSpecialCollectionsRoom.JPG/440px-UFHistoricBuildingSmathersLibraryEastInteriorSpecialCollectionsRoom.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UFHistoricBuildingSmathersLibraryEastInteriorSpecialCollectionsRoom.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Smathers Library, first opened in 1926, is the oldest library at the university</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/George_A._Smathers_Libraries" title="George A. Smathers Libraries">George A. Smathers Libraries</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/George_A._Smathers_Libraries" title="George A. Smathers Libraries">George A. Smathers Libraries</a> at the University of Florida is one of the largest university library systems in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup> In total, the University of Florida has ten libraries, and over 5.3 million volumes of books and journals and 7 million microfilms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MediaGuide_109-6"><a href="#cite_note-MediaGuide-109">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup> Collections cover virtually all disciplines and include a wide array of formats – from books and journals to manuscripts, maps, and recorded music. Increasingly collections are digital and are accessible on the Internet via the library web page or the library catalog.</p>
<p>The numerous libraries provide primary support to all academic programs except those served by the <a class="external text" href="http://www.library.health.ufl.edu/" rel="nofollow">Health Science Center Library</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Lawton_Chiles_Legal_Information_Center" title="Lawton Chiles Legal Information Center">Lawton Chiles Legal Information Center</a>. In 2006, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_Library_West" title="University of Florida Library West">Library West</a> went through a $30 million renovation that doubled capacity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup> This facility is now better equipped to handle the information technology necessities that students need to complete their studies. Such progress is represented by its state-of-the-art Information Commons,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup> which offers production studios, digital media computing areas, and a presentation area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[136]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Florida_buildings" title="List of University of Florida buildings">List of University of Florida buildings</a></div>
<p>The University of Florida campus encompasses over 2,000 acres (8.1 km<sup>2</sup>). The campus is home to many notable structures, such as <a href="/wiki/Century_Tower_(University_of_Florida)" title="Century Tower (University of Florida)">Century Tower</a>, a 157-foot (48 m) tall <a href="/wiki/Carillon" title="Carillon">carillon</a> tower in the center of the historic district. Other notable facilities include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J._Hillis_Miller_Health_Science_Center" title="J. Hillis Miller Health Science Center">Health Science Center</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steve_Spurrier-Florida_Field_at_Ben_Hill_Griffin_Stadium" title="Steve Spurrier-Florida Field at Ben Hill Griffin Stadium">Steve Spurrier-Florida Field at Ben Hill Griffin Stadium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Library_East_(Gainesville,_Florida)" title="Library East (Gainesville, Florida)">Smathers Library</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curtis_M._Phillips_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Curtis M. Phillips Center for the Performing Arts">Phillips Center for the Performing Arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samuel_P._Harn_Museum_of_Art" title="Samuel P. Harn Museum of Art">Harn Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_Auditorium_(Gainesville,_Florida)" title="University Auditorium (Gainesville, Florida)">University Auditorium</a>, <a href="/wiki/O%27Connell_Center" title="O'Connell Center">O'Connell Center</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Hub_(Gainesville,_Florida)" title="The Hub (Gainesville, Florida)">The Hub</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Reitz_Union">The Reitz Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: The Reitz Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Reitz is the campus union at the University of Florida. On February 1, 2016, it was reopened after an extensive renovation and expansion. The 138,000 square feet of new space includes support space for student organizations, new lounges, study spaces, a game room and dance studios.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historic_sites">Historic sites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Historic sites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A number of the University of Florida's buildings are historically significant. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_Campus_Historic_District" title="University of Florida Campus Historic District">University of Florida Campus Historic District</a> comprises 19 buildings and encompasses approximately 650 acres (2.6 km<sup>2</sup>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OCHP_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-OCHP-141">[139]</a></sup> Two buildings outside the historic district, the <a href="/wiki/Old_WRUF_Radio_Station" title="Old WRUF Radio Station">old WRUF radio station</a> (now the university police station) and <a href="/wiki/Norman_Hall_(Gainesville,_Florida)" title="Norman Hall (Gainesville, Florida)">Norman Hall</a> (formerly the P.K. Yonge Laboratory School), are also listed on the historic register.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup> The buildings on the U.S. National Register of Historic Places for their architectural or historic significance are:</p>
