<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="PaCE">PaCE</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: PaCE">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>UF launched a new program in the fall of 2015 called PaCE, or Pathway to Campus Enrollment. PaCE was designed to provide an alternative way to enroll students who would have been accepted through regular admissions, but there is not enough space in dorms or classrooms. To be accepted into the PaCE program, you would have been accepted to UF initially. PaCE was randomly given to admitted students based on major. Through PaCE, students are admitted to UF, but are required to complete 60 credit hours and all of their prerequisite courses through UF online before transitioning to on-campus learning. The University of Florida admitted 2420 students for PaCE for the class of 2021.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Innovation_Academy">Innovation Academy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Innovation Academy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Innovation Academy at UF is a program designed for students that want to focus on innovation, creativity, leadership, and entrepreneurship along with their intended major. Students that enroll in the Innovation Academy go to UF during the spring and summer semesters so that they can participate in internships and study abroad opportunities during the fall. IA covers 30 different majors that all share a common minor-Innovation. UF recently admitted 979 students into the Innovation Academy for the class of 2021.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fraternities_and_sororities">Fraternities and sororities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Fraternities and sororities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Approximately 5,200 undergraduate students (or approximately 15%) are members of either a sorority or fraternity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sorority" title="Sorority">Sorority</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities">Fraternity</a> Affairs (formerly known as Greek Life) at the University of Florida is separated into four divisions: <a href="/wiki/North-American_Interfraternity_Conference" title="North-American Interfraternity Conference">Interfraternity Council</a> (IFC), <a href="/wiki/National_Panhellenic_Conference" title="National Panhellenic Conference">National Panhellenic Conference</a> (NPC), <a href="/wiki/National_Multicultural_Greek_Council" title="National Multicultural Greek Council">Multicultural Greek Council</a> (MGC), and the <a href="/wiki/National_Pan-Hellenic_Council" title="National Pan-Hellenic Council">National Pan-Hellenic Council</a> (NPHC). The <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Omega" title="Order of Omega">Order of Omega</a> has a chapter at the university.</p>
<p>The Interfraternity Council (IFC) comprises 25 fraternities, and the Panhellenic Council is made up of 17 sororities. Some of the fraternity chapters on campus are older than the university itself, with the first chapters being chartered in 1884 and founded on the campus of one of the university's predecessor institutions in Lake City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Multicultural Greek Council consists of 12 cultural organizations (<a href="/wiki/Latino" title="Latino">Latino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asian</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asian</a>, etc.), seven fraternities and five sororities. The National Pan-Hellenic Council comprises nine historically black organizations, five fraternities and four sororities.</p>
<p>There are also three Greek service organizations for students, two sororities Delta Nu Zeta and <a href="/wiki/Omega_Phi_Alpha" title="Omega Phi Alpha">Omega Phi Alpha</a> and one fraternity, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi_Omega" title="Alpha Phi Omega">Alpha Phi Omega</a>.</p>
<p>There are now also four university recognized organizations for Christian students, <a href="/wiki/Beta_Upsilon_Chi" title="Beta Upsilon Chi">Beta Upsilon Chi</a> and Kappa Phi Epsilon fraternities as well as <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Phi_Lambda" title="Sigma Phi Lambda">Sigma Phi Lambda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christian_sorority" title="Christian sorority">Theta Alpha</a> sororities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>In early 2015 the Panhellenic Council announced the arrival of two new sororities. Gamma Phi Beta was chartered in Fall 2015 and Alpha Phi will start recruitment in Fall 2017. Construction is underway on Sorority Row for Gamma Phi Beta's house.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dance_Marathon_at_UF">Dance Marathon at UF</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Dance Marathon at UF">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dance Marathon at UF is an annual 26.2-hour event benefiting the patients of <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_Health" title="University of Florida Health">University of Florida Health</a> Shands Children's Hospital in Gainesville, Florida.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup> Each year, more than 800 students stay awake and on their feet to raise money and awareness for Children's Miracle Network Hospitals. In the 23 years of Dance Marathon at UF's existence, more than $15 million has been donated, making it the most successful student-run philanthropy in the southeastern United States. In 2017, DM at UF raised a record total of $2,724,324 for UF Health Shands Children's Hospital, becoming the second most successful Dance Marathon in the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reserve_Officer_Training_Corps">Reserve Officer Training Corps</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Reserve Officer Training Corps">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_ROTC" title="University of Florida ROTC">University of Florida ROTC</a></div>
<p>The University of Florida <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reserve_Officer_Training_Corps" title="Reserve Officer Training Corps">Reserve Officer Training Corps</a> is the official <a href="/wiki/Officer_(armed_forces)" title="Officer (armed forces)">officer</a> training and commissioning program at the University of Florida. Officially founded in 1905, it is one of the oldest such programs in the nation.</p>
<p>The Reserve Officer Training Corps offers commissions for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">United States Marine Corps</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">United States Air Force</a>. The unit is one of the oldest in the nation, and is at <a href="/wiki/Van_Fleet_Hall_(Gainesville,_Florida)" title="Van Fleet Hall (Gainesville, Florida)">Van Fleet Hall</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Reserve Officer Training Corps at the University of Florida offers training in the military sciences to students who desire to perform military service after they graduate. The Departments of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Army" title="U.S. Army">Army</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Air_Force" title="U.S. Air Force">Air Force</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" title="U.S. Navy">Navy</a> each maintain a Reserve Officers Training Corps and each individual department has a full staff of military personnel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[152]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">Housing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Housing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UF-BeatyTowers.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/UF-BeatyTowers.JPG/200px-UF-BeatyTowers.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/UF-BeatyTowers.JPG/300px-UF-BeatyTowers.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/UF-BeatyTowers.JPG/400px-UF-BeatyTowers.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UF-BeatyTowers.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Beaty Towers at UF house the IA Living Learning Community</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_student_housing" title="University of Florida student housing">University of Florida student housing</a></div>
<p>The University of Florida provides over 9,200 students with housing in residence halls and complexes on the eastern and western sides of campus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup> Facilities vary in the cost of rent and privacy. Housing plans also offer students access to dining facilities. The university also provides housing to a number of graduate students and their families.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup> As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the university is building a new residence hall on campus that will be more accessible to students with disabilities.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recreation_and_Fitness_on_Campus">Recreation and Fitness on Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Recreation and Fitness on Campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UF-RecreationalAreaAtBroward.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/UF-RecreationalAreaAtBroward.JPG/200px-UF-RecreationalAreaAtBroward.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/UF-RecreationalAreaAtBroward.JPG/300px-UF-RecreationalAreaAtBroward.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/UF-RecreationalAreaAtBroward.JPG/400px-UF-RecreationalAreaAtBroward.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UF-RecreationalAreaAtBroward.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Recreational complex near Broward Hall.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The University of Florida's Department of Recreational Sports (<a class="external text" href="http://recsports.ufl.edu/" rel="nofollow">RecSports</a>) includes operation of two lake-front parks at Lake Wauburg, group fitness, personal and small group training, massage therapy, intramural sports, 48 competitive sports clubs, two world-class indoor fitness and recreation facilities, four campus pools, outdoor rock climbing, an adventure travel recreation program, campus fields and facilities, a skate park and staff development services for over 700 students who are employed by the department's programs.</p>
<p>RecSports manages the <a class="external text" href="http://recsports.ufl.edu/locations/southwest-recreation-center" rel="nofollow">University of Florida Southwest Recreation Center</a>, a 140,000 square foot (13,000 m²) state-of-the-art facility with six indoor basketball courts, a split-level cardio room, personal training studio, massage therapy rooms, 14,000 square foot (1,300 m²) strength and conditioning area and a social lounge with a smoothie bar. Other campus facilities operated by RecSports include the <a class="external text" href="http://recsports.ufl.edu/locations/student-recreation-fitness-center" rel="nofollow">Student Recreation &amp; Fitness Center</a> and <a class="external text" href="http://recsports.ufl.edu/locations/broward-outdoor-recreation-complex" rel="nofollow">Broward Outdoor Recreation Complex</a>.</p>
<p>Outside of RecSports, campus recreation options include an arts and crafts center, bowling alley and game room—all located in the J. Wayne Reitz Union--, and the Mark Bostick Golf Course.</p>
<p>The campus also contains nature trails, open spaces, small ponds, picnic areas, shady nooks and an 81-acre (330,000 m<sup>2</sup>) wildlife sanctuary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FU_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-FU-157">[155]</a></sup></p>
<p>The UF Scientific Diver Development Program provides SCUBA training for students interested in pursuing a career involving underwater research.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_government">Student government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Student government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UFSG.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="324" data-file-width="324" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/56/UFSG.png/200px-UFSG.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/56/UFSG.png/300px-UFSG.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/56/UFSG.png 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UFSG.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Seal for the UF Student Government</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The University of Florida <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Student_Government" title="Student Government">Student Government</a> is the governing body of students who attend the University of Florida, representing the university's nearly 50,000 undergraduate, graduate and professional students. The university's student government operates on a yearly $18.7 million budget, one of the largest student government budgets in the United States, and the money is allocated by the Budget Committee of the Student Senate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup></p>
<p>The student government was established in 1909 and consists of executive, judicial and unicameral legislative branches. The executive branch includes the student government president, vice president and treasurer elected by the student body during the spring semester, as well as nine agencies and forty-one cabinet members.</p>
<p>The Student Senate is the legislative branch, and is composed of 100 senators who serve one-year terms. The student body elects fifty senators during each spring semester and the remaining fifty during the fall semester. The senators elect a Senate President and Senate President Pro Tempore twice a year, after each semester's elections, to lead the Student Senate. During student government elections students may also vote on referendums, such as the renewable energy referendum,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gators_for_a_Sustainable_Campus_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gators_for_a_Sustainable_Campus-160">[158]</a></sup> which was approved by 78% of voting students in the spring of 2007. This referendum proposed a fifty-cents-per-credit-hour increase to student activity fees to fund renewable energy and efficiency on campus.</p>
<p>The student government judicial branch has two major components: the Supreme Court of the Student Body (headed by a Chief Justice) and all elections related officials (the Supervisor of Elections and the Elections Commission). The Supreme Court consists of seven second or third-year law students nominated by the Student Body President and confirmed by the Student Senate. Each justice serves a "life-time" term, which extends through the individual justice's graduation and insulates the court from the politics of student government. The Chief Justice may appoint a marshal and clerk. The election commission is also composed of law students and it adjudicates all student government election complaints. The commission has six members, one of whom also serves as the commission chairman.</p>
<p>The student government executive branch is led by the Student Body President and includes the Student Body Vice President, Student Body Treasurer, twelve agencies, twelve executive secretaries, nineteen cabinet directors, and three cabinet chairs.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alma_mater">Alma mater</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Alma mater">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Alma_mater_(song)" title="Alma mater (song)">alma mater</a> for the University of Florida was composed by Milton Yeats in 1925.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[159]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus_and_area_transportation">Campus and area transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Campus and area transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The university campus is served by nine bus routes of the <a href="/wiki/Gainesville_Regional_Transit_System" title="Gainesville Regional Transit System">Gainesville Regional Transit System</a> (RTS). Students, faculty, and staff with university-issued ID cards are able to use the system for no additional fee. RTS also provides other campus services, including Gator Aider (during football games), S.N.A.P, and Later Gator nighttime service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[160]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Gainesville region and the university are served by the <a href="/wiki/Gainesville_Regional_Airport" title="Gainesville Regional Airport">Gainesville Regional Airport</a>, which is located in the northeast portion of Gainesville and has daily flights to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miami,_Florida" title="Miami, Florida">Miami</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlanta,_Georgia" title="Atlanta, Georgia">Atlanta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[161]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_media">Student media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Student media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The University of Florida community includes six major student-run media outlets and companion Web sites.</p>
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent_Florida_Alligator" title="The Independent Florida Alligator">The Independent Florida Alligator</a></i> is the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Student_newspaper" title="Student newspaper">student-run newspaper</a> in the United States, and operates without oversight from the university administration.</li>
<li><i>The Really Independent Florida Crocodile</i>, a <a href="/wiki/Parody" title="Parody">parody</a> of the Alligator, is a monthly magazine started by students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[162]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WRUF_(AM)" title="WRUF (AM)">WRUF</a> (850 AM and 95.3 FM) (www.wruf.com) includes ESPN programming, local sports news and talk programming produced by the station's professional staff and the latest local sports news produced by the college's Innovation News Center.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WRUF-FM" title="WRUF-FM">WRUF-FM</a> (103.7 FM) broadcasts country music and attracts an audience from the <a href="/wiki/Gainesville,_Florida" title="Gainesville, Florida">Gainesville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ocala,_Florida" title="Ocala, Florida">Ocala</a> areas.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WRUF-LD" title="WRUF-LD">WRUF-LD</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Low-power_broadcasting" title="Low-power broadcasting">low-power</a> television station that carries weather, news, and sports programming.</li>
<li>WUFT (www.wuft.org) is a PBS member station with a variety of programming that includes a daily student-produced newscast.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WUFT-FM" title="WUFT-FM">WUFT-FM</a> (89.1 FM) is an NPR member radio station which airs news and public affairs programming, including student-produced long-form news reporting. WUFT-FM's programming also airs on WJUF-FM (90.1). In addition, WUFT offers 24-hour classical/arts programming on 92.1.</li>
</ul>
<p>Various other journals and magazines are published by the university's academic units and student groups, including the literary journal <i><a href="/wiki/Subtropics_(journal)" title="Subtropics (journal)">Subtropics</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[163]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_placement">Career placement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Career placement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The University of Florida Career Resource Center is located in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J._Wayne_Reitz_Student_Union" title="J. Wayne Reitz Student Union">Reitz Student Union</a>. Its mission is to assist students and alumni who are seeking career development, career experiences, and employment opportunities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[164]</a></sup> These services involve on and off-campus job interviews, career planning, assistance in applying to graduate and professional schools, and internship and co-op placements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[165]</a></sup> The Career Resource Center offers workshops, information sessions, career fairs, and advisement on future career options. Staff also counsel students and alumni regarding resumes and portfolios, interviewing tactics, cover letters, job strategies and other potential leads for finding employment in the corporate, academic and government sectors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[166]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/The_Princeton_Review" title="The Princeton Review">The Princeton Review</a> ranked the Career Resource Center as the best among 368 ranked universities in career and job placement services in 2010,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-princetonreview.com_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-princetonreview.com-169">[167]</a></sup> and fourth overall in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-princetonreview.com_169-1"><a href="#cite_note-princetonreview.com-169">[167]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UF_HarnMuseum.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/UF_HarnMuseum.JPG/200px-UF_HarnMuseum.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/UF_HarnMuseum.JPG/300px-UF_HarnMuseum.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/UF_HarnMuseum.JPG/400px-UF_HarnMuseum.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UF_HarnMuseum.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Samuel_P._Harn_Museum_of_Art" title="Samuel P. Harn Museum of Art">Harn Museum of Art</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UF_FloridaMuseumOfNaturalHistory.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/UF_FloridaMuseumOfNaturalHistory.jpg/200px-UF_FloridaMuseumOfNaturalHistory.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/UF_FloridaMuseumOfNaturalHistory.jpg/300px-UF_FloridaMuseumOfNaturalHistory.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/UF_FloridaMuseumOfNaturalHistory.jpg/400px-UF_FloridaMuseumOfNaturalHistory.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UF_FloridaMuseumOfNaturalHistory.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Florida_Museum_of_Natural_History" title="Florida Museum of Natural History">Museum of Natural History</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Florida_Museum_of_Natural_History" title="Florida Museum of Natural History">Florida Museum of Natural History</a>, established in 1891, is one of the country's oldest natural history museums and was officially chartered by the State of <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[168]</a></sup> This facility is dedicated to understanding, preserving and interpreting biological diversity and cultural heritage. In over 100 years of operations the Florida Museum of Natural History has been housed in several buildings, from the <a href="/wiki/Seagle_Building" title="Seagle Building">Seagle Building</a> to facilities at Dickinson Hall, Powell Hall, and the Randell Research Center. In 2000 the McGuire Center for Lepidoptera and Biodiversity was opened after a generous donation from University of Florida benefactors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[169]</a></sup> The McGuire Center houses a collection of more than six million butterfly and moth specimens, making it one of the largest collections of <a href="/wiki/Lepidoptera" title="Lepidoptera">Lepidoptera</a> in the world, rivaling the <a href="/wiki/Natural_History_Museum,_London" title="Natural History Museum, London">Natural History Museum</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London,_England" title="London, England">London, England</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[170]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Samuel_P._Harn_Museum_of_Art" title="Samuel P. Harn Museum of Art">Samuel P. Harn Museum of Art</a>, established in 1990, is also located at the University of Florida on the southwest part of campus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[171]</a></sup> This facility is one of the largest university art museums in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">South</a>, the Harn has more than 7,000 works in its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Collection_(museum)" title="Collection (museum)">permanent collection</a> and an array of temporary exhibitions. The museum's permanent collections are focused on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_art" title="Asian art">Asian</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_art" title="African art">African</a>, <a href="/wiki/Modern_art" title="Modern art">modern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_art" title="Contemporary art">contemporary art</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Photography" title="Photography">photography</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup> The university sponsors educational programs at the museum including films, lectures, interactive activities, and school and family offerings. In October 2005 the Harn expanded by more than 18,000 square feet (1,700 m<sup>2</sup>) with the opening of the Mary Ann Harn Cofrin Pavilion, which includes new educational and meeting areas and the Camellia Court Cafe, the first eatery for visitors of the Cultural Plaza.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[173]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Performing_arts_and_music">Performing arts and music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Performing arts and music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UF_Phillips_Center.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/UF_Phillips_Center.JPG/200px-UF_Phillips_Center.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/UF_Phillips_Center.JPG/300px-UF_Phillips_Center.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/UF_Phillips_Center.JPG/400px-UF_Phillips_Center.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UF_Phillips_Center.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Curtis_M._Phillips_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Curtis M. Phillips Center for the Performing Arts">Phillips Center</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Performing_arts" title="Performing arts">Performing arts</a> venues at the University of Florida consist of the <a href="/wiki/Curtis_M._Phillips_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Curtis M. Phillips Center for the Performing Arts">Curtis M. Phillips Center for the Performing Arts</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_Auditorium_(Gainesville,_Florida)" title="University Auditorium (Gainesville, Florida)">University Auditorium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constans_Theatre" title="Constans Theatre">Constans Theatre</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Baughman_Center" title="Baughman Center">Baughman Center</a>, and performances at the <a href="/wiki/O%27Connell_Center" title="O'Connell Center">O'Connell Center</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[174]</a></sup> The mission is to provide an unparalleled experience where performing artists create and share knowledge to serve the student body, faculty, and staff at the university; Gainesville residents; and visitors to North Central Florida.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[175]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_Auditorium_(Gainesville,_Florida)" title="University Auditorium (Gainesville, Florida)">University Auditorium</a> was founded in the mid-1920s and is home to the Anderson Memorial Organ. The auditorium has a concert stage and can seat up to 843 patrons. The venue is suitable for <a href="/wiki/Concert" title="Concert">musical concerts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lecture" title="Lecture">special lectures</a>, <a href="/wiki/Convocation" title="Convocation">convocations</a>, dance concerts, and pageants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[176]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UniversityAuditorium.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="500" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b7/UniversityAuditorium.jpg/200px-UniversityAuditorium.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b7/UniversityAuditorium.jpg/300px-UniversityAuditorium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b7/UniversityAuditorium.jpg/400px-UniversityAuditorium.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UniversityAuditorium.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/University_Auditorium_(Gainesville,_Florida)" title="University Auditorium (Gainesville, Florida)">University Auditorium</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Curtis_M._Phillips_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Curtis M. Phillips Center for the Performing Arts">Phillips Center for the Performing Arts</a> was founded in 1992 and is a performing arts <a href="/wiki/Theatre" title="Theatre">theatre</a>. The Phillips Center is on the western side of campus, and hosts established and emerging national and international artists on the main stage, as well as the annual <a href="/wiki/Miss_University_of_Florida" title="Miss University of Florida">Miss University of Florida</a> pageant and performances by the University of Florida's original student-run dance company, Floridance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[177]</a></sup> The Phillips Center consists of a 1,700-seat <a href="/wiki/Proscenium" title="Proscenium">proscenium hall</a> and the 200-seat Squitieri Studio Theatre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[178]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Constans_Theatre" title="Constans Theatre">Constans Theatre</a> was founded in 1967 and is a performing arts venue next to the <a href="/wiki/J._Wayne_Reitz_Union" title="J. Wayne Reitz Union">J. Wayne Reitz Union</a>. Constans Theatre serves as a venue for musical concerts, theater, dance, and lectures, and is a sub-venue of the Nadine McGuire Pavilion and Dance Pavilion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[179]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Baughman_Center" title="Baughman Center">Baughman Center</a> was founded in 2000 and serves as a venue for small musical and performing arts events. The facility consists of two buildings next to <a href="/wiki/Lake_Alice_(Gainesville,_Florida)" title="Lake Alice (Gainesville, Florida)">Lake Alice</a> on the western portion of campus. The main building is a 1,500-square-foot (140 m<sup>2</sup>) pavilion, while the other is a 1,000-square-foot (93 m<sup>2</sup>) administrative building. The Baughman Center can accommodate up to 96 patrons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The University of Florida has been portrayed in several books,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[181]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[182]</a></sup> movies<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup> and television shows. In addition, the University of Florida campus has been the backdrop for a number of different books and movies. <a href="/wiki/Robert_Cade" title="Robert Cade">Robert Cade</a>, a professor in the university's <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_College_of_Medicine" title="University of Florida College of Medicine">College of Medicine</a>, was the leader of the research team that invented the ubiquitous sports drink <a href="/wiki/Gatorade" title="Gatorade">Gatorade</a> as a hydration supplement for the Florida Gators football team in 1965–66.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[184]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Florida_Gators" title="Florida Gators">Florida Gators</a></div>
<dl>
<dd><i>For individual articles on the Florida Gators team in each sport, see the table at right.</i></dd>
</dl>
<p>The University of Florida's intercollegiate sports teams, known as the "<a href="/wiki/Florida_Gators" title="Florida Gators">Florida Gators</a>," compete in <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a> (NCAA) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference" title="Southeastern Conference">Southeastern Conference</a> (SEC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[185]</a></sup> The Gators compete in nine men's sports and twelve women's sports.</p>
<p>For the 2014–15 school year, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_Athletic_Association" title="University of Florida Athletic Association">University Athletic Association</a> budgeted more $100 million for its sports teams and facilities. Since 1987–88, the Gators have won twenty-three of the last twenty-six SEC All-Sports Trophies, recognizing Florida as the best overall athletics program in the SEC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[186]</a></sup> Florida is the only program in the nation to finish among the nation's top ten in each of the last thirty national all-sports standings and is the only SEC school to place 100 or more student-athletes on the Academic Honor Roll each of the last fifteen years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[187]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Florida Gators have won a total of thirty-five national team championships,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[188]</a></sup> thirty of which are NCAA championships. Florida Gators athletes have also won 267 NCAA championships in individual sports events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[189]</a></sup> Florida is one of only two Division I FBS universities to win multiple national championships in each of the two most popular NCAA sports: football (1996, 2006, 2008) and men's basketball (2006, 2007).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Florida_Gators_football" title="Florida Gators football">Florida Gators football</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BenHillGriffinStadium.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1970" data-file-width="3076" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/BenHillGriffinStadium.png/220px-BenHillGriffinStadium.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/BenHillGriffinStadium.png/330px-BenHillGriffinStadium.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/BenHillGriffinStadium.png/440px-BenHillGriffinStadium.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BenHillGriffinStadium.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aerial of <a href="/wiki/Ben_Hill_Griffin_Stadium" title="Ben Hill Griffin Stadium">Ben Hill Griffin Stadium</a>, also known as "The Swamp."</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The University of Florida fielded its first official varsity football team in the fall of 1906, when the university held its first classes on its new Gainesville campus. Since then, the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Gators_football" title="Florida Gators football">Florida Gators football</a> team has played in 40 bowl games, won three consensus national championships and eight <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference" title="Southeastern Conference">Southeastern Conference</a> (SEC) championships, produced 89 first-team All-Americans, 45 <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a> (NFL) first-round draft choices, and three <a href="/wiki/Heisman_Trophy" title="Heisman Trophy">Heisman Trophy</a> winners.</p>
<p>The Gators won their first post-season game on January 1, 1953, beating Tulsa 14-13 in Jacksonville, Florida. The Gators' first major bowl win was the 1967 <a href="/wiki/Orange_Bowl" title="Orange Bowl">Orange Bowl</a> in which coach <a href="/wiki/Ray_Graves" title="Ray Graves">Ray Graves</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heisman_Trophy" title="Heisman Trophy">Heisman Trophy</a> quarterback <a href="/wiki/Steve_Spurrier" title="Steve Spurrier">Steve Spurrier</a> led the Gators to a 27–12 victory over the <a href="/wiki/Georgia_Tech_Yellow_Jackets_football" title="Georgia Tech Yellow Jackets football">Georgia Tech Yellow Jackets</a>.</p>
<p>In 1990, Spurrier returned to his <a href="/wiki/Alma_mater" title="Alma mater">alma mater</a> as its new head coach, and spurred the Gators to their first six official SEC football championships. The Gators, quarterbacked by their second Heisman Trophy winner, <a href="/wiki/Danny_Wuerffel" title="Danny Wuerffel">Danny Wuerffel</a>, won their first national championship in 1996 with a 52–20 victory over <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Seminoles_football" title="Florida State Seminoles football">Florida State Seminoles</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1997_Sugar_Bowl" title="1997 Sugar Bowl">Sugar Bowl</a>. In 2006, <a href="/wiki/Urban_Meyer" title="Urban Meyer">Urban Meyer</a> coached the Gators to a 13–1 record, capturing their seventh <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SEC_Championship" title="SEC Championship">SEC Championship</a>, and defeating the top-ranked <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Buckeyes_football" title="Ohio State Buckeyes football">Ohio State Buckeyes</a> 41–14 for the <a href="/wiki/2007_BCS_National_Championship_Game" title="2007 BCS National Championship Game">BCS National Championship</a>. In 2008, the Gators' third Heisman-winning quarterback, <a href="/wiki/Tim_Tebow" title="Tim Tebow">Tim Tebow</a>, led them in a 24–14 <a href="/wiki/2009_BCS_National_Championship_Game" title="2009 BCS National Championship Game">BCS Championship Game</a> victory over the <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_Sooners_football" title="Oklahoma Sooners football">Oklahoma Sooners</a> for the team's third national championship.</p>
<p>Since 1930, the Gators' home field has been Florida Field at <a href="/wiki/Ben_Hill_Griffin_Stadium" title="Ben Hill Griffin Stadium">Ben Hill Griffin Stadium</a>, which seats 88,548 fans. The stadium is popularly known as "The Swamp."</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">Basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Basketball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Florida_Gators_men%27s_basketball" title="Florida Gators men's basketball">Florida Gators men's basketball</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:O%27Connell_Center.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/O%27Connell_Center.jpg/200px-O%27Connell_Center.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/O%27Connell_Center.jpg/300px-O%27Connell_Center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/O%27Connell_Center.jpg/400px-O%27Connell_Center.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:O%27Connell_Center.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Interior view of the <a href="/wiki/O%27Connell_Center" title="O'Connell Center">O'Connell Center</a>, configured for basketball.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Florida_Gators_men%27s_basketball" title="Florida Gators men's basketball">Florida Gators men's basketball</a> team has also gained national recognition over the past twenty years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[190]</a></sup> The Gators went to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Final_Four" title="Final Four">Final Four</a> of the 1994 NCAA tournament under coach <a href="/wiki/Lon_Kruger" title="Lon Kruger">Lon Kruger</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[191]</a></sup> and coach <a href="/wiki/Billy_Donovan" title="Billy Donovan">Billy Donovan</a> led the Gators back to the NCAA Final Four in 2000, losing to the <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_Spartans_men%27s_basketball" title="Michigan State Spartans men's basketball">Michigan State Spartans</a> in the final. Under Donovan, the Gators won their first Southeastern Conference (SEC) tournament championship in 2005, beating the <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Wildcats_men%27s_basketball" title="Kentucky Wildcats men's basketball">Kentucky Wildcats</a>. After repeating as SEC tournament champions in 2006, the Gators won their first basketball national championship, defeating the <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Bruins" title="UCLA Bruins">UCLA Bruins</a> 73–57 in the final game of the NCAA basketball tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[192]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Gators beat the <a href="/wiki/Arkansas_Razorbacks_men%27s_basketball" title="Arkansas Razorbacks men's basketball">Arkansas Razorbacks</a> 77–56 to win their third consecutive SEC tournament title in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[193]</a></sup> Florida defeated Ohio State 84–75 to again win the NCAA basketball tournament championship.</p>
<p>The Gators play their home games in the <a href="/wiki/O%27Connell_Center" title="O'Connell Center">O'Connell Center</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[194]</a></sup> The 11,548-seat multi-purpose indoor arena was completed in 1980, and is popularly known as the "O'Dome."</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Olympics">Olympics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Olympics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Florida_Olympians" title="List of University of Florida Olympians">List of University of Florida Olympians</a></div>
<p>Since 1968, 163 Gator athletes and 13 Florida coaches have represented 37 countries in the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a>, winning 50 Olympic gold medals, 28 silver medals and 30 bronze medals through the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[195]</a></sup> The list of University of Florida alumni who are Olympic gold medalists includes <a href="/wiki/Brad_Wilkerson" title="Brad Wilkerson">Brad Wilkerson</a> (baseball); <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delisha_Milton-Jones" title="Delisha Milton-Jones">Delisha Milton-Jones</a> (basketball); <a href="/wiki/Steve_Mesler" title="Steve Mesler">Steve Mesler</a> (bobsled); <a href="/wiki/Heather_Mitts" title="Heather Mitts">Heather Mitts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abby_Wambach" title="Abby Wambach">Abby Wambach</a> (soccer); <a href="/wiki/Theresa_Andrews" title="Theresa Andrews">Theresa Andrews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catie_Ball" title="Catie Ball">Catie Ball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tracy_Caulkins" title="Tracy Caulkins">Tracy Caulkins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matt_Cetlinski" title="Matt Cetlinski">Matt Cetlinski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Conor_Dwyer" title="Conor Dwyer">Conor Dwyer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geoff_Gaberino" title="Geoff Gaberino">Geoff Gaberino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Haislett" title="Nicole Haislett">Nicole Haislett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Heath_(swimmer)" title="Mike Heath (swimmer)">Mike Heath</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Larson" title="David Larson">David Larson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Lochte" title="Ryan Lochte">Ryan Lochte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Nesty" title="Anthony Nesty">Anthony Nesty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dara_Torres" title="Dara Torres">Dara Torres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Wayte" title="Mary Wayte">Mary Wayte</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martin_Zubero" title="Martin Zubero">Martin Zubero</a> (swimming); and <a href="/wiki/Kerron_Clement" title="Kerron Clement">Kerron Clement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Mitchell" title="Dennis Mitchell">Dennis Mitchell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Shorter" title="Frank Shorter">Frank Shorter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_Taylor_(athlete)" title="Christian Taylor (athlete)">Christian Taylor</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bernard_Williams_(athlete)" title="Bernard Williams (athlete)">Bernard Williams</a> (track and field).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni">Notable alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Notable alumni">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Florida_alumni" title="List of University of Florida alumni">List of University of Florida alumni</a></div>
<p>The University of Florida has more than 330,000 alumni. Over 57,000 are dues-paying members of the University of Florida Alumni Association. Florida alumni live in every state and more than 100 foreign countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[196]</a></sup> Florida alumni include two <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> winners, ten <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">U.S. Senators</a>, forty-two <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">U.S. Representatives</a>, eight <a href="/wiki/Ambassadors_of_the_United_States" title="Ambassadors of the United States">U.S. ambassadors</a>, eleven <a href="/wiki/Governor_(United_States)" title="Governor (United States)">state governors</a>, eleven state supreme court justices, and over fifty federal court judges. Florida graduates have served as the executive leaders of such diverse institutions as the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">U.S. Marine Corps</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Organization_for_Women" title="National Organization for Women">National Organization for Women</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_faculty">Notable faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Notable faculty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Florida_faculty_and_administrators" title="List of University of Florida faculty and administrators">List of University of Florida faculty and administrators</a></div>
<p>Awards won by University of Florida faculty members include a <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medal</a>, numerous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prizes" title="Pulitzer Prizes">Pulitzer Prizes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>'s top award for research, and the Smithsonian Institution's conservation award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[197]</a></sup> There are more than sixty eminent scholar endowed faculty chairs, and more than fifty faculty elections to the National Academy of Sciences, Engineering, or Arts and Sciences, the Institute of Medicine or a counterpart in a foreign nation. More than two dozen faculty are members of the National Academies of Science and Engineering and the Institute of Medicine or counterpart in a foreign nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MediaGuide_109-7"><a href="#cite_note-MediaGuide-109">[107]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="President_Fuchs">President Fuchs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: President Fuchs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dr. W. Kent Fuchs is the president at the University of Florida. He became the 12th president in January 2015. Fuchs earned a doctorate in electrical and computer engineering at the University of Illinois. He became a professor at the University of Illinois. Fuchs then became the head of the electrical and computer engineering school at Purdue and then the provost at Cornell University for six years before taking his position at Florida.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[198]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The motto of UF was written by James Nesbitt Anderson, first Dean of the College of Arts &amp; Sciences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This is the year classes began at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Florida_Seminary" title="East Florida Seminary">East Florida Seminary</a>, the oldest of the four institutions that were consolidated to create the modern University of Florida in 1905. This date was set by the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Board_of_Control" title="Florida Board of Control">Florida Board of Control</a> in 1935; previously the university traced its founding date to 1905, when the predecessor institutions were merged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[2]</a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
</div>
</div>

<li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-22">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The present university campus incorporates much of the former seminary and academy campuses. <a href="/wiki/Epworth_Hall_(Gainesville,_Florida)" title="Epworth Hall (Gainesville, Florida)">Epworth Hall</a>, one of the main building of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_University_of_Florida" title="History of the University of Florida">East Florida Seminary</a>, still stands in downtown Gainesville, but is not within the boundaries of the university's campus.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">University of Florida, <a class="external text" href="http://www.ufl.edu/150/htmltimeline/1853_1905.html/" rel="nofollow">UF Timeline</a> <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20070210211910/http://www.ufl.edu/150/htmltimeline/1853_1905.html" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> 2007-02-10 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>.. The name, the "University of Florida," has been held by three separate schools: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Florida_Seminary" title="West Florida Seminary">West Florida Seminary</a> was renamed the "University of Florida" by the legislature, and held the name from 1883 to 1902; Florida Agricultural College was renamed in 1902 and held the name until 1905; and the name of the new University of the State of Florida was simplified to the University of Florida in 1909. The West Florida Seminary was a predecessor to the modern <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_University" title="Florida State University">Florida State University</a> in Tallahassee.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-24">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">University of Florida, Department of Housing, <a class="external text" href="http://www.housing.ufl.edu/housing/Facilities_TourPages/buckman.htm/" rel="nofollow">Buckman Hall Quick Facts</a>. Retrieved April 18, 2012.</span></li>
